keys","childPages":[]},{"href":"/en/rest/users/users","title":"Users","childPages":[]}]}],"layout":"product-landing"},"status":200,"xHost":"docs.github.com"},"articleContext":{"title":"Getting started with the REST API","intro":"\u003cp\u003eLearn how to use the GitHub REST API.\u003c/p\u003e","effectiveDate":"","renderedPage":"\u003ch2 id=\"introduction\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#introduction\"\u003eIntroduction\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis article describes how to use the GitHub REST API with GitHub CLI, \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e, or JavaScript. For a quickstart guide, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/quickstart\"\u003eQuickstart for GitHub REST API\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-tool curl\"\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"about-requests-to-the-rest-api\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#about-requests-to-the-rest-api\"\u003eAbout requests to the REST API\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis section describes the elements that make up an API request:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ca href=\"#http-method\"\u003eHTTP method\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ca href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ca href=\"#headers\"\u003eHeaders\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ca href=\"#media-types\"\u003eMedia types\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ca href=\"#authentication\"\u003eAuthentication\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ca href=\"#parameters\"\u003eParameters\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEvery request to the REST API includes an HTTP method and a path. Depending on the REST API endpoint, you might also need to specify request headers, authentication information, query parameters, or body parameters.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe REST API reference documentation describes the HTTP method, path, and parameters for every endpoint. It also displays example requests and responses for each endpoint. For more information, see the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest\"\u003eREST reference documentation\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"http-method\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#http-method\"\u003eHTTP method\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe HTTP method of an endpoint defines the type of action it performs on a given resource. Some common HTTP methods are \u003ccode\u003eGET\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003ePOST\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eDELETE\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003ePATCH\u003c/code\u003e. The REST API reference documentation provides the HTTP method for every endpoint.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the HTTP method for the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/issues/issues#list-repository-issues\"\u003e\"List repository issues\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e is \u003ccode\u003eGET\u003c/code\u003e.\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhere possible, the GitHub REST API strives to use an appropriate HTTP method for each action.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eGET\u003c/code\u003e: Used for retrieving resources.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ePOST\u003c/code\u003e: Used for creating resources.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ePATCH\u003c/code\u003e: Used for updating properties of resources.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003ePUT\u003c/code\u003e: Used for replacing resources or collections of resources.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003ccode\u003eDELETE\u003c/code\u003e: Used for deleting resources.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"path\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEach endpoint has a path. The REST API reference documentation gives the path for every endpoint. For example, the path for the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/issues/issues#list-repository-issues\"\u003e\"List repository issues\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e is \u003ccode\u003e/repos/{owner}/{repo}/issues\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe curly brackets \u003ccode\u003e{}\u003c/code\u003e in a path denote path parameters that you need to specify. Path parameters modify the endpoint path and are required in your request. For example, the path parameters for the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/issues/issues#list-repository-issues\"\u003e\"List repository issues\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e are \u003ccode\u003e{owner}\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e{repo}\u003c/code\u003e. To use this path in your API request, replace \u003ccode\u003e{repo}\u003c/code\u003e with the name of the repository where you would like to request a list of issues, and replace \u003ccode\u003e{owner}\u003c/code\u003e with the name of the account that owns the repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"headers\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#headers\"\u003eHeaders\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eHeaders provide extra information about the request and the desired response. Following are some examples of headers that you can use in your requests to the GitHub REST API. For an example of a request that uses headers, see \u003ca href=\"#making-a-request\"\u003eMaking a request\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"accept\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#accept\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMost GitHub REST API endpoints specify that you should pass an \u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e header with a value of \u003ccode\u003eapplication/vnd.github+json\u003c/code\u003e. The value of the \u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e header is a media type. For more information about media types, see \u003ca href=\"#media-types\"\u003eMedia types\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"x-github-api-version\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#x-github-api-version\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eX-GitHub-Api-Version\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou should use this header to specify a version of the REST API to use for your request. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/overview/api-versions\"\u003eAPI Versions\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"user-agent\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#user-agent\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAll API requests must include a valid \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e header. The \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e header identifies the user or application that is making the request.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-tool cli\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBy default, GitHub CLI sends a valid \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e header. However, GitHub recommends using your GitHub username, or the name of your application, for the \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e header value. This allows GitHub to contact you if there are problems.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-tool curl\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBy default, \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e sends a valid \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e header. However GitHub recommends using your GitHub username, or the name of your application, for the \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e header value. This allows GitHub to contact you if there are problems.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-tool javascript\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you use the Octokit.js SDK, the SDK will send a valid \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e header for you. However, GitHub recommends using your GitHub username, or the name of your application, for the \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e header value. This allows GitHub to contact you if there are problems.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe following is an example \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e for an app named \u003ccode\u003eAwesome-Octocat-App\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-shell\"\u003eUser-Agent: Awesome-Octocat-App\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eRequests with no \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e header will be rejected. If you provide an invalid \u003ccode\u003eUser-Agent\u003c/code\u003e header, you will receive a \u003ccode\u003e403 Forbidden\u003c/code\u003e response.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ca name=\"media-types\"\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"media-types\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#media-types\"\u003eMedia types\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can specify one or more media types by adding them to the \u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e header of your request. For more information about the \u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e header, see \u003ca href=\"#accept\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMedia types specify the format of the data you want to consume from the API. Media types are specific to resources, allowing them to change independently and support formats that other resources don't. The documentation for each GitHub REST API endpoint will describe the media types that it supports. For more information, see the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest\"\u003eGitHub REST API documentation\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe most common media types supported by the GitHub REST API are \u003ccode\u003eapplication/vnd.github+json\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003eapplication/json\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThere are custom media types that you can use with some endpoints. For example, the REST API to manage \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/commits/commits#get-a-commit\"\u003ecommits\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/pulls/pulls\"\u003epull requests\u003c/a\u003e support the media types \u003ccode\u003ediff\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003epatch\u003c/code\u003e, and \u003ccode\u003esha\u003c/code\u003e. The media types \u003ccode\u003efull\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003eraw\u003c/code\u003e, \u003ccode\u003etext\u003c/code\u003e, or \u003ccode\u003ehtml\u003c/code\u003e are used by some other endpoints.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAll custom media types for GitHub look like this: \u003ccode\u003eapplication/vnd.github.PARAM+json\u003c/code\u003e, where \u003ccode\u003ePARAM\u003c/code\u003e is the name of the media type. For example, to specify the \u003ccode\u003eraw\u003c/code\u003e media type, you would use \u003ccode\u003eapplication/vnd.github.raw+json\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor an example of a request that uses media types, see \u003ca href=\"#making-a-request\"\u003eMaking a request\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"authentication\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#authentication\"\u003eAuthentication\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMany endpoints require authentication or return additional information if you are authenticated. Additionally, you can make more requests per hour when you are authenticated.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-tool curl\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo authenticate your request, you will need to provide an authentication token with the required scopes or permissions. There a few different ways to get a token: You can create a personal access token, generate a token with a GitHub App, or use the built-in \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e in a GitHub Actions workflow. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/overview/authenticating-to-the-rest-api\"\u003eAuthenticating to the REST API\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor an example of a request that uses an authentication token, see \u003ca href=\"#making-a-request\"\u003eMaking a request\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-accent\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eNote\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nIf you don't want to create a token, you can use GitHub CLI. GitHub CLI will take care of authentication for you, and help keep your account secure. For more information, see the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/guides/getting-started-with-the-rest-api?tool=cli\"\u003eGitHub CLI version of this page\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-attention\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M6.457 1.047c.659-1.234 2.427-1.234 3.086 0l6.082 11.378A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.082 15H1.918a1.75 1.75 0 0 1-1.543-2.575Zm1.763.707a.25.25 0 0 0-.44 0L1.698 13.132a.25.25 0 0 0 .22.368h12.164a.25.25 0 0 0 .22-.368Zm.53 3.996v2.5a.75.75 0 0 1-1.5 0v-2.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0ZM9 11a1 1 0 1 1-2 0 1 1 0 0 1 2 0Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eWarning\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nTreat your access token the same way you would treat your passwords or other sensitive credentials. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/overview/keeping-your-api-credentials-secure\"\u003eKeeping your API credentials secure\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-tool cli\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAlthough some REST API endpoints are accessible without authentication, GitHub CLI requires you to authenticate before you can use the \u003ccode\u003eapi\u003c/code\u003e subcommand to make an API request. Use the \u003ccode\u003eauth login\u003c/code\u003e subcommand to authenticate to GitHub. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#making-a-request\"\u003eMaking a request\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-tool javascript\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo authenticate your request, you will need to provide an authentication token with the required scopes or permissions. There a few different ways to get a token: You can create a personal access token, generate a token with a GitHub App, or use the built-in \u003ccode\u003eGITHUB_TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e in a GitHub Actions workflow. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/overview/authenticating-to-the-rest-api\"\u003eAuthenticating to the REST API\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor an example of a request that uses an authentication token, see \u003ca href=\"#making-a-request\"\u003eMaking a request\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-alert ghd-alert-attention\" data-container=\"alert\"\u003e\u003cp class=\"ghd-alert-title\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon mr-2\" aria-hidden\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M6.457 1.047c.659-1.234 2.427-1.234 3.086 0l6.082 11.378A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.082 15H1.918a1.75 1.75 0 0 1-1.543-2.575Zm1.763.707a.25.25 0 0 0-.44 0L1.698 13.132a.25.25 0 0 0 .22.368h12.164a.25.25 0 0 0 .22-.368Zm.53 3.996v2.5a.75.75 0 0 1-1.5 0v-2.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0ZM9 11a1 1 0 1 1-2 0 1 1 0 0 1 2 0Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003eWarning\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\nTreat your access token the same way you would treat your passwords or other sensitive credentials. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/overview/keeping-your-api-credentials-secure\"\u003eKeeping your API credentials secure\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"parameters\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#parameters\"\u003eParameters\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMany API methods require or allow you to send additional information in parameters in your request. There are a few different types of parameters: Path parameters, body parameters, and query parameters.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"path-parameters\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#path-parameters\"\u003ePath parameters\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003ePath parameters modify the endpoint path. These parameters are required in your request. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"body-parameters\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#body-parameters\"\u003eBody parameters\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBody parameters allow you to pass additional data to the API. These parameters can be optional or required, depending on the endpoint. For example, a body parameter may allow you to specify an issue title when creating a new issue, or specify certain settings when enabling or disabling a feature. The documentation for each GitHub REST API endpoint will describe the body parameters that it supports. For more information, see the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest\"\u003eGitHub REST API documentation\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/issues/issues#create-an-issue\"\u003e\"Create an issue\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e requires that you specify a title for the new issue in your request. It also allows you to optionally specify other information, such as text to put in the issue body, users to assign to the new issue, or labels to apply to the new issue. For an example of a request that uses body parameters, see \u003ca href=\"#making-a-request\"\u003eMaking a request\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou must authenticate your request to pass body parameters. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#authenticating\"\u003eAuthenticating\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"query-parameters\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#query-parameters\"\u003eQuery parameters\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eQuery parameters allow you to control what data is returned for a request. These parameters are usually optional. The documentation for each GitHub REST API endpoint will describe any query parameters that it supports. For more information, see the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest\"\u003eGitHub REST API documentation\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/activity/events#list-public-events\"\u003e\"List public events\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e returns thirty issues by default. You can use the \u003ccode\u003eper_page\u003c/code\u003e query parameter to return two issues instead of 30. You can use the \u003ccode\u003epage\u003c/code\u003e query parameter to fetch only the first page of results. For an example of a request that uses query parameters, see \u003ca href=\"#making-a-request\"\u003eMaking a request\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"making-a-request\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#making-a-request\"\u003eMaking a request\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-tool cli\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis section demonstrates how to make an authenticated request to the GitHub REST API using GitHub CLI.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"1-setup\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#1-setup\"\u003e1. Setup\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eInstall GitHub CLI on macOS, Windows, or Linux. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/cli/cli#installation\"\u003eInstallation\u003c/a\u003e in the GitHub CLI repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"2-authenticate\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#2-authenticate\"\u003e2. Authenticate\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003col\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo authenticate to GitHub, run the following command from your terminal.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-shell\"\u003egh auth login\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use the \u003ccode\u003e--scopes\u003c/code\u003e option to specify what scopes you want. If you want to authenticate with a token that you created, you can use the \u003ccode\u003e--with-token\u003c/code\u003e option. For more information, see the \u003ca href=\"https://cli.github.com/manual/gh_auth_login\"\u003eGitHub CLI \u003ccode\u003eauth login\u003c/code\u003e documentation\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSelect where you want to authenticate to:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf you access GitHub at GitHub.com, select \u003cstrong\u003eGitHub.com\u003c/strong\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf you access GitHub at a different domain, select \u003cstrong\u003eOther\u003c/strong\u003e, then enter your hostname (for example: \u003ccode\u003eoctocorp.ghe.com\u003c/code\u003e).\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFollow the rest of the on-screen prompts.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eGitHub CLI automatically stores your Git credentials for you when you choose HTTPS as your preferred protocol for Git operations and answer \"yes\" to the prompt asking if you would like to authenticate to Git with your GitHub credentials. This can be useful as it allows you to use Git commands like \u003ccode\u003egit push\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003egit pull\u003c/code\u003e without needing to set up a separate credential manager or use SSH.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"3-choose-an-endpoint-for-your-request\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#3-choose-an-endpoint-for-your-request\"\u003e3. Choose an endpoint for your request\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003col\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eChoose an endpoint to make a request to. You can explore GitHub's \u003ca href=\"/en/rest\"\u003eREST API documentation\u003c/a\u003e to discover endpoints that you can use to interact with GitHub.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIdentify the HTTP method and path of the endpoint. You will send these with your request. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#http-method\"\u003eHTTP method\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/issues/issues#create-an-issue\"\u003e\"Create an issue\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e uses the HTTP method \u003ccode\u003ePOST\u003c/code\u003e and the path \u003ccode\u003e/repos/{owner}/{repo}/issues\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIdentify any required path parameters. Required path parameters appear in curly brackets \u003ccode\u003e{}\u003c/code\u003e in the path of the endpoint. Replace each parameter placeholder with the desired value. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/issues/issues#create-an-issue\"\u003e\"Create an issue\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e uses the path \u003ccode\u003e/repos/{owner}/{repo}/issues\u003c/code\u003e, and the path parameters are \u003ccode\u003e{owner}\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e{repo}\u003c/code\u003e. To use this path in your API request, replace \u003ccode\u003e{repo}\u003c/code\u003e with the name of the repository where you would like to create a new issue, and replace \u003ccode\u003e{owner}\u003c/code\u003e with the name of the account that owns the repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"4-make-a-request-with-github-cli\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#4-make-a-request-with-github-cli\"\u003e4. Make a request with GitHub CLI\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse the GitHub CLI \u003ccode\u003eapi\u003c/code\u003e subcommand to make your API request. For more information, see the \u003ca href=\"https://cli.github.com/manual/gh_api\"\u003eGitHub CLI \u003ccode\u003eapi\u003c/code\u003e documentation\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn your request, specify the following options and values:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e--method\u003c/strong\u003e followed by the HTTP method and the path of the endpoint. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#http-method\"\u003eHTTP method\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e--header:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/strong\u003e Pass the media type in an \u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e header. To pass multiple media types in an \u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e header, separate the media types with a comma: \u003ccode\u003eAccept: application/vnd.github+json,application/vnd.github.diff\u003c/code\u003e. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#accept\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#media-types\"\u003eMedia types\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003eX-GitHub-Api-Version\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/strong\u003e Pass the API version in a \u003ccode\u003eX-GitHub-Api-Version\u003c/code\u003e header. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#x-github-api-version\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eX-GitHub-Api-Version\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003e-f\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e or \u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003e-F\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e followed by any body parameters or query parameters in \u003ccode\u003ekey=value\u003c/code\u003e format. Use the \u003ccode\u003e-F\u003c/code\u003e option to pass a parameter that is a number, Boolean, or null. Use the \u003ccode\u003e-f\u003c/code\u003e option to pass string parameters.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSome endpoints use query parameters that are arrays. To send an array in the query string, use the query parameter once per array item, and append \u003ccode\u003e[]\u003c/code\u003e after the query parameter name. For example, to provide an array of two repository IDs, use \u003ccode\u003e-f repository_ids[]=REPOSITORY_A_ID -f repository_ids[]=REPOSITORY_B_ID\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you do not need to specify any body parameters or query parameters in your request, omit this option. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#body-parameters\"\u003eBody parameters\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#query-parameters\"\u003eQuery parameters\u003c/a\u003e. For examples, see \u003ca href=\"#example-request-using-body-parameters\"\u003eExample request using body parameters\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#example-request-using-query-parameters\"\u003eExample request using query parameters\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"example-request\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-request\"\u003eExample request\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e to return the octocat as ASCII art.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"code-example\"\u003e\u003cheader class=\"d-flex flex-items-center flex-justify-between p-2 text-small endpoint\u003c/a\u003e to create a new issue in the octocat/Spoon-Knife repository. \\\n\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/header\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-shell\"\u003egh api --method POST /repos/octocat/Spoon-Knife/issues \\\n--header \"Accept: application/vnd.github+json\" \\\n--header \"X-GitHub-Api-Version: 2022-11-28\" \\\n-f title='Created with the REST API' \\\n-f body='This is a test issue created by the REST API' \\\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-tool curl\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis section demonstrates how to make an authenticated request to the GitHub REST API using \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"1-setup-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#1-setup-1\"\u003e1. Setup\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou must have \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e installed on your machine. To check if \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e is already installed, run \u003ccode\u003ecurl --version\u003c/code\u003e on the command line.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf the output provides information about the version of \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e, that means \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e is installed.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eIf you get a message similar to \u003ccode\u003ecommand not found: curl\u003c/code\u003e, that means \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e is not installed. Download and install \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"https://curl.se/download.html\"\u003ethe curl download page\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"2-choose-an-endpoint-for-your-request\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#2-choose-an-endpoint-for-your-request\"\u003e2. Choose an endpoint for your request\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003col\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eChoose an endpoint to make a request to. You can explore GitHub's \u003ca href=\"/en/rest\"\u003eREST API documentation\u003c/a\u003e to discover endpoints that you can use to interact with GitHub.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIdentify the HTTP method and path of the endpoint. You will send these with your request. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#http-method\"\u003eHTTP method\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/issues/issues#create-an-issue\"\u003e\"Create an issue\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e uses the HTTP method \u003ccode\u003ePOST\u003c/code\u003e and the path \u003ccode\u003e/repos/{owner}/{repo}/issues\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIdentify any required path parameters. Required path parameters appear in curly brackets \u003ccode\u003e{}\u003c/code\u003e in the path of the endpoint. Replace each parameter placeholder with the desired value. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/issues/issues#create-an-issue\"\u003e\"Create an issue\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e uses the path \u003ccode\u003e/repos/{owner}/{repo}/issues\u003c/code\u003e, and the path parameters are \u003ccode\u003e{owner}\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e{repo}\u003c/code\u003e. To use this path in your API request, replace \u003ccode\u003e{repo}\u003c/code\u003e with the name of the repository where you would like to create a new issue, and replace \u003ccode\u003e{owner}\u003c/code\u003e with the name of the account that owns the repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"3-create-authentication-credentials\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#3-create-authentication-credentials\"\u003e3. Create authentication credentials\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eCreate an access token to authenticate your request. You can save your token and use it for multiple requests. Give the token any scopes or permissions that are required to access the endpoint. You will send this token in an \u003ccode\u003eAuthorization\u003c/code\u003e header with your request. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#authentication\"\u003eAuthentication\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"4-make-a-curl-request\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#4-make-a-curl-request\"\u003e4. Make a \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e request\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUse the \u003ccode\u003ecurl\u003c/code\u003e command to make your request. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"https://curl.se/docs/manpage.html\"\u003ethe curl documentation\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSpecify the following options and values in your request:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--request\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003e-X\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e followed by the HTTP method as the value. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#http-method\"\u003eHTTP method\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--url\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e followed by the full path as the value. The full path is a URL that includes the base URL for the GitHub REST API (\u003ccode\u003ehttps://api.github.com\u003c/code\u003e) and the path of the endpoint, like this: \u003ccode\u003ehttps://api.github.com/PATH\u003c/code\u003e. Replace \u003ccode\u003ePATH\u003c/code\u003e with the path of the endpoint. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo use query parameters, add a \u003ccode\u003e?\u003c/code\u003e to the end of the path, then append your query parameter name and value in the form \u003ccode\u003eparameter_name=value\u003c/code\u003e. Separate multiple query parameters with \u003ccode\u003e\u0026#x26;\u003c/code\u003e. If you need to send an array in the query string, use the query parameter once per array item, and append \u003ccode\u003e[]\u003c/code\u003e after the query parameter name. For example, to provide an array of two repository IDs, use \u003ccode\u003e?repository_ids[]=REPOSITORY_A_ID\u0026#x26;repository_ids[]=REPOSITORY_B_ID\u003c/code\u003e. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#query-parameters\"\u003eQuery parameters\u003c/a\u003e. For an example, see \u003ca href=\"#example-request-using-query-parameters-1\"\u003eExample request using query parameters\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--header\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003e-H\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/strong\u003e Pass the media type in an \u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e header. To pass multiple media types in an \u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e header, separate the media types with a comma, for example: \u003ccode\u003eAccept: application/vnd.github+json,application/vnd.github.diff\u003c/code\u003e. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#accept\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#media-types\"\u003eMedia types\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003eX-GitHub-Api-Version\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/strong\u003e Pass the API version in a \u003ccode\u003eX-GitHub-Api-Version\u003c/code\u003e header. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#x-github-api-version\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003eX-GitHub-Api-Version\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003eAuthorization\u003c/code\u003e:\u003c/strong\u003e Pass your authentication token in an \u003ccode\u003eAuthorization\u003c/code\u003e header. Note that in most cases you can use \u003ccode\u003eAuthorization: Bearer\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003eAuthorization: token\u003c/code\u003e to pass a token. However, if you are passing a JSON web token (JWT), you must use \u003ccode\u003eAuthorization: Bearer\u003c/code\u003e. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#authentication\"\u003eAuthentication\u003c/a\u003e. For an example of a request that uses an \u003ccode\u003eAuthorization\u003c/code\u003e header, see \u003ca href=\"#example-request-using-body-parameters-1\"\u003eExample request using body parameters\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003e\u003ccode\u003e--data\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003e-d\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/strong\u003e followed by any body parameters within a JSON object. If you do not need to specify any body parameters in your request, omit this option. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#body-parameters\"\u003eBody parameters\u003c/a\u003e. For an example, see \u003ca href=\"#example-request-using-body-parameters-1\"\u003eExample request using body parameters\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"example-request-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-request-1\"\u003eExample request\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe following example request uses the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/meta/meta#get-octocat\"\u003e\"Get Octocat\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e to return the octocat as ASCII art.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"code-example\"\u003e\u003cheader class=\"d-flex flex-items-center flex-justify-between p-2 text-small rounded-top-1 border-top border-left border-right\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"flex-1\"\u003eShell\u003c/span\u003e\u003cbutton class=\"js-btn-copy btn btn-sm tooltipped tooltipped-nw\" aria-label=\"Copy Shell code to clipboard\" data-clipboard=\"2503540538\"\u003e\u003csvg version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" class=\"octicon octicon-copy\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M0 6.75C0 5.784.784 5 1.75 5h1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-1.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-1.5a.75.75 0 0 1 1.5 0v1.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 9.25 16h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 0 14.25Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003cpath d=\"M5 1.75C5 .784 5.784 0 6.75 0h7.5C15.216 0 16 .784 16 1.75v7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 14.25 11h-7.5A1.75 1.75 0 0 1 5 9.25Zm1.75-.25a.25.25 0 0 0-.25.25v7.5c0 .138.112.25.25.25h7.5a.25.25 0 0 0 .25-.25v-7.5a.25.25 0 0 0-.25-.25Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/button\u003e\u003cpre hidden data-clipboard=\"2503540538\"\u003ecurl --request GET \\\n--url \"https://api.github.com/octocat\" \\\n--header \"Accept: application/vnd.github+json\" \\\n--header \"X-GitHub-Api-Version: 2022-11-28\"\n\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/header\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-shell\"\u003ecurl --request GET \\\n--url \"https://api.github.com/octocat\" \\\n--header \"Accept: application/vnd.github+json\" \\\n--header \"X-GitHub-Api-Version: 2022-11-28\"\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"example-request-using-query-parameters-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#example-request-using-query-parameters-1\"\u003eExample request using query parameters\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/activity/events#list-public-events\"\u003e\"List public events\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e returns thirty issues by default. javascript\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis section demonstrates how to make a request to the GitHub REST API using JavaScript and \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/octokit/octokit.js\"\u003eOctokit.js\u003c/a\u003e. Setup\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou must install \u003ccode\u003eoctokit\u003c/code\u003e to use the Octokit.js library shown in the following examples.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eInstall \u003ccode\u003eoctokit\u003c/code\u003e. For example, \u003ccode\u003enpm install octokit\u003c/code\u003e. For other ways to install or load \u003ccode\u003eoctokit\u003c/code\u003e, see \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/octokit/octokit.js/#readme\"\u003ethe Octokit.js README\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"2-choose-an-endpoint-for-your-request-1\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#2-choose-an-endpoint-for-your-request-1\"\u003e2. Choose an endpoint for your request\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003col\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eChoose an endpoint to make a request to. You can explore GitHub's \u003ca href=\"/en/rest\"\u003eREST API documentation\u003c/a\u003e to discover endpoints that you can use to interact with GitHub.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIdentify the HTTP method and path of the endpoint. You will send these with your request. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#http-method\"\u003eHTTP method\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/issues/issues#create-an-issue\"\u003e\"Create an issue\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e uses the HTTP method \u003ccode\u003ePOST\u003c/code\u003e and the path \u003ccode\u003e/repos/{owner}/{repo}/issues\u003c/code\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIdentify any required path parameters. Required path parameters appear in curly brackets \u003ccode\u003e{}\u003c/code\u003e in the path of the endpoint. Replace each parameter placeholder with the desired value. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#path\"\u003ePath\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, the \u003ca href=\"/en/rest/issues/issues#create-an-issue\"\u003e\"Create an issue\" endpoint\u003c/a\u003e uses the path \u003ccode\u003e/repos/{owner}/{repo}/issues\u003c/code\u003e, and the path parameters are \u003ccode\u003e{owner}\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003e{repo}\u003c/code\u003e. To use this path in your API request, replace \u003ccode\u003e{repo}\u003c/code\u003e with the name of the repository where you would like to create a new issue, and replace \u003ccode\u003e{owner}\u003c/code\u003e with the name of the account that owns the repository.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ol\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"3-create-an-access-token\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#3-create-an-access-token\"\u003e3. Create an access token\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eCreate an access token to authenticate your request. You can save your token and use it for multiple requests. Give the token any scopes or permissions that are required to access the endpoint. You will send this token in an \u003ccode\u003eAuthorization\u003c/code\u003e header with your request. For more information, see \u003ca href=\"#authentication\"\u003eAuthentication\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 id=\"4-make-a-request-with-octokitjs\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#4-make-a-request-with-octokitjs\"\u003e4. Make a request with Octokit.js\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003col\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eImport \u003ccode\u003eoctokit\u003c/code\u003e in your script. For example, \u003ccode\u003eimport { Octokit } from \"octokit\";\u003c/code\u003e. For other ways to import \u003ccode\u003eoctokit\u003c/code\u003e, see \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/octokit/octokit.js/#readme\"\u003ethe Octokit.js README\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eCreate an instance of \u003ccode\u003eOctokit\u003c/code\u003e with your token. Replace \u003ccode\u003eYOUR-TOKEN\u003c/code\u003e with your token.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"code-example\"\u003e\u003cheader class=\"d-flex flex-items-center flex-justify-between p-2 To pass additional headers or a different \u003ccode\u003eAccept\u003c/code\u003e header, add a \u003ccode\u003eheaders\u003c/code\u003e property to the object that is passed as a second argument. aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEvery request will return an HTTP status code that indicates the success of the response. For more information about response codes, see \u003ca href=\"https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/Status\"\u003ethe MDN HTTP response status code documentation\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAdditionally, the response will include headers that give more details about the response. Headers that start with \u003ccode\u003eX-\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003ex-\u003c/code\u003e are custom to GitHub. For example, the \u003ccode\u003ex-ratelimit-remaining\u003c/code\u003e and \u003ccode\u003ex-ratelimit-reset\u003c/code\u003e headers tell you how many requests you can make in a time period.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ghd-tool cli\"\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo view the status code and headers, use the \u003ccode\u003e--include\u003c/code\u003e or \u003ccode\u003e--i\u003c/code\u003e option when you send your request.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor example, this request gets a list of issues in the octocat/Spoon-Knife repository:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-shell\"\u003egh api \\\n--header 'Accept: application/vnd.github+json' \\\n--method GET /repos/octocat/Spoon-Knife/issues \\\n-F per_page=2 --include\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAnd it returns a response code and headers that look something like this:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-shell\"\u003eHTTP/2.0 200 OK\nAccess-Control-Allow-Origin: *\nAccess-Control-Expose-Headers: ETag, Link, Location, Retry-After, X-RateLimit-Limit, X-RateLimit-Remaining, X-RateLimit-Used, X-RateLimit-Resource, X-RateLimit-Reset, X-OAuth-Scopes, X-Accepted-OAuth-Scopes, X-Poll-Interval, X-GitHub-Media-Type, X-GitHub-SSO, X-GitHub-Request-Id, Deprecation, Sunset\nCache-Control: private, max-age=60, s-maxage=60\nContent-Security-Policy: default-src 'none'\nContent-Type: application/json; If an error occurs, the promise resolves to an object that includes the HTTP status code of the response (\u003ccode\u003estatus\u003c/code\u003e) and the response headers (\u003ccode\u003eresponse.headers\u003c/code\u003e).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can use a \u003ccode\u003etry/catch\u003c/code\u003e block to catch an error if it occurs. data.json\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe previous two commands return something like:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003e\"title\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-punctuation\"\u003e:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"Edit index file\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-punctuation\"\u003e,\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"hljs-attr\"\u003e\"authorID\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-punctuation\"\u003e:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e53709285\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-punctuation\"\u003e}\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor more information about jq, see \u003ca href=\"https://stedolan.github.io/jq/\"\u003ethe jq documentation\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"detailed-versus-summary-representations\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#detailed-versus-summary-representations\"\u003eDetailed versus summary representations\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eA response can include all attributes for a resource or only a subset of attributes, depending on whether you fetch an individual resource or a list of resources.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWhen you fetch an \u003cem\u003eindividual resource\u003c/em\u003e, like a specific repository, the response will typically include all attributes for that resource. This is the \"detailed\" representation of the resource.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eWhen you fetch a \u003cem\u003elist of resources\u003c/em\u003e, like a list of multiple repositories, the response will only include a subset of the attributes for each resource. This is the \"summary\" representation of the resource.\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNote that authorization sometimes influences the amount of detail included in a representation.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe reason for this is because some attributes are computationally expensive for the API to provide, so GitHub excludes those attributes from the summary representation. To obtain those attributes, you can fetch the detailed representation.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe documentation provides an example response for each API method. The example response illustrates all attributes that are returned by that method.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch4 id=\"hypermedia\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#hypermedia\"\u003eHypermedia\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h4\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAll resources may have one or more \u003ccode\u003e*_url\u003c/code\u003e properties linking to other resources. These are meant to provide explicit URLs so that proper API clients don't need to construct URLs on their own. It is highly recommended that API clients use these. Doing so will make future upgrades of the API easier for developers. All URLs are expected to be proper \u003ca href=\"https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc6570\"\u003eRFC 6570\u003c/a\u003e URI templates.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can then expand these templates using something like the \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/hannesg/uri_template\"\u003euri_template\u003c/a\u003e gem:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cpre\u003e\u003ccode class=\"hljs language-ruby\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"hljs-meta prompt_\"\u003e\u003e\u003e\u003c/span\u003e tmpl = \u003cspan class=\"hljs-title class_\"\u003eURITemplate\u003c/span\u003e.new(\u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e'/notifications{?since,all,participating}'\u003c/span\u003e)\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-meta prompt_\"\u003e\u003e\u003e\u003c/span\u003e tmpl.expand\n=\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"/notifications\"\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-meta prompt_\"\u003e\u003e\u003e\u003c/span\u003e tmpl.expand \u003cspan class=\"hljs-symbol\"\u003eall:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e1\u003c/span\u003e\n=\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"/notifications?all=1\"\u003c/span\u003e\n\n\u003cspan class=\"hljs-meta prompt_\"\u003e\u003e\u003e\u003c/span\u003e tmpl.expand \u003cspan class=\"hljs-symbol\"\u003eall:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e1\u003c/span\u003e, \u003cspan class=\"hljs-symbol\"\u003eparticipating:\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-number\"\u003e1\u003c/span\u003e\n=\u003e \u003cspan class=\"hljs-string\"\u003e\"/notifications?all=1\u0026#x26;participating=1\"\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\n\u003ch2 id=\"next-steps\" tabindex=\"-1\"\u003e\u003ca class=\"heading-link\" href=\"#next-steps\"\u003eNext steps\u003cspan class=\"heading-link-symbol\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis article demonstrated how to list and create issues in a repository. For more practice, try to comment on an issue, edit the title of an issue, or close an issue.
